**GT: 0.782414626*sin(t) - 0.083425*vВі - 0.995417*log(|v| + 1)**

Let me analyze the key components of the GT:
1. A sin(t) term
2. A -vВі term
3. A -log(|v| + 1) term

The log(|v| + 1) term is the tricky part. Let me check candidates that have log-like terms.

**Candidate 1:** Has `c7*log(c8*exp(c9*vВІ) + 1)`. If c9=0, this becomes `c7*log(c8+1)`, a constant. Can't reproduce log(|v|+1).

**Candidate 21:** `c0 + c1*t + c2*v + c3*v*log(c4*Abs(v) + 1) + c5*exp(c6*t)*sin(c7*t + c8)`

This has `v*log(c4*|v| + 1)`, not `log(|v| + 1)`. These are different functions of v. Setting c6=0 gives sin term as constant. The exp*sin term with c6=0 gives a constant. So we'd have: constant + c1*t + c2*v + c3*v*log(c4|v|+1) + constant*sin(constant). This can't reproduce log(|v|+1) without the v multiplier.

**Candidate 42:** `c0*t + c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1)`

Setting c3=0: `c0*t + c1 + c2*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1)`

Setting c0=0, c4=1, c5=0: `c1 + c2*sin(t) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1)`

This is a single log expression вҖ” it can't produce both vВі and log(|v|+1) terms. So no.

**Candidate 13:** `c0*exp(c1/(c2 + t)) + c3 + c4*v + c5*v*|v| + c6*log(c7*vВІ + 1)*sin(c8*t + c9)`

**Candidate 44:** `c0*t + c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*v^c7*exp(c8*t)`
